================================================================================
SECTION 10: PI CONTROLLER FULL DECOMPILATION
================================================================================

  Three tightly-coupled functions implement the AFC closed-loop PI controller:
    0x340A0  afc_pi_output_stage  — computes P and I gain coefficients
    0x342A8  afc_pi_controller    — error computation and state machine
    0x3439E  afc_enable_gate      — conditional enable/disable
    0x343CE  afc_output_clamp     — final output clamping

─── 0x342A8: afc_pi_controller — ERROR + STATE MACHINE ─────────────────────

  ENTRY:
    GBR = 0xFFFF77C8           ; AFC correction state base
    FR4 = [FFFF6540]           ; sensor input (front O2 signal)

  PSEUDOCODE:

    mode = byte[FFFF7448]          ; CL/OL mode flag (1=CL, else=OL)
    prev_state = byte[GBR+0x9D]   ; previous PI state (FFFF7865)
    sub_state = byte[GBR+0x60]    ; sub-state (FFFF7828)
    current_corr = float[FFFF77C8] ; current AFC correction accumulator

    if (mode != 1) goto STATE_OL   ; not in CL → skip PI

    ; ── CL MODE ──
    if (prev_state != 0) {
        ; EXISTING CORRECTION — check limits
        limit_hi = float[CC004]     ; = 20.0 (max AFC correction %)
        current_out = float[FFFF7814]  ; current PI output
        if (current_out > limit_hi) {
            state = 2               ; needs rich correction
            goto CHECK_LOW
        }
    CHECK_LOW:
        limit_lo = float[CC008]     ; = 0.0 (min / dead band)
        if (limit_lo > current_out) {
            state = 3               ; needs lean correction
        } else {
            state = 4               ; within limits, no action
        }
    } else {
        ; FRESH CL ENTRY (prev_state == 0)
        if (sub_state != 1) goto FINALIZE

        ; ── COMPUTE ERROR ──
        error = sensor_input - current_corr     ; fsub at 0x342DA
        [stack] = error                          ; save for later

        ; ── P GAIN LOOKUP ──
        P_correction = table_lookup_BEAB0(error) ; jsr 0xBEAB0
        threshold = float[CC000]                 ; = 2.0
        if (P_correction > threshold) {
            ; P correction exceeds 2.0 → use raw FPUL
            output = FPUL
        } else {
            ; P correction <= 2.0 → use error directly
            output = error
        }
        [FFFF7814] = output              ; store PI output
        state = 1                         ; normal update
    }

  STATE_OL:                               ; mode != 1
    if (sub_state == 1) {
        [FFFF7814] = FPUL                 ; freeze current value
    }
    state = 4                             ; disabled

  FINALIZE (switch on state):
    case 1:  ; Normal PI update
        [FFFF7818] = [FFFF7814]           ; copy output to accumulator
        byte[GBR+0x62] = 1               ; FFFF782A = active flag
    case 2:  ; Rich correction needed
        correction = [FFFF7818]
        correction = correction - 1.0     ; subtract CC00C (=1.0)
        result = table_lookup_BE960(correction)  ; rich interp
        [FFFF7818] = result
    case 3:  ; Lean correction needed
        correction = [FFFF7818]
        correction = correction + 1.0     ; add CC00C (=1.0)
        result = table_lookup_BE970(correction)  ; lean interp
        [FFFF7818] = result
    case 4:  ; Disabled / no correction
        [FFFF7818] = FPUL                 ; store current FPUL

    byte[GBR+0x9D] = mode                ; save state for next cycle (FFFF7865)
    return

  KEY INSIGHT: The PI controller uses the error between sensor input and
  current correction (not between sensor and target AFR). The 2.0 threshold
  at CC000 acts as a P-gain limiter — if the table lookup returns > 2.0,
  the raw FPUL value is used instead of the computed error. The 1.0 value
  at CC00C is the step size for rich/lean correction ramp.

  STATE MACHINE SUMMARY:
    State 0: First CL entry — compute fresh error, do P lookup
    State 1: Normal — copy new output to accumulator
    State 2: Rich limit exceeded (>20%) — step down by 1.0, re-interpolate
    State 3: Lean limit exceeded (<0%) — step up by 1.0, re-interpolate
    State 4: Disabled or within deadband — freeze output

─── 0x340A0: afc_pi_output_stage — P AND I GAIN COMPUTATION ───────────────

  INPUTS (loaded at entry):
    FR12 = [FFFF6624]     MAF (alternate/computed)
    FR15 = [FFFF6350]     RPM
    FR14 = [FFFF63F8]     MAF (primary sensor)
    FR13 = [FFFF68DC]     load variable
    FR9  = [FFFF78B0]     CL/OL state variable (saved to stack)
    FR8  = [FFFF65FC]     condition variable (saved to stack)

  ENABLE CHECK:
    flag_A = byte[FFFF8E7E]
    flag_B = byte[FFFF85D7]
    if (flag_A != 1) skip entire PI computation → jump to 0x3427E

  PSEUDOCODE:

    ; ── PROPORTIONAL PATH ──
    ; Each lookup calls interpolation function at 0xBE830
    P_gain_A = interp_1D(desc=0xACEA0, input=RPM)        ; ECT-axis table
    P_gain_B = interp_1D(desc=0xACEB4, input=load_var)    ; load-axis table
    P_norm   = interp_1D(desc=0xAC4FC, input=CL_state)    ; airflow/state-axis

    proportional = (P_gain_A + P_gain_B) * P_norm

    ; ── INTEGRAL PATH ──
    I_comp   = interp_2D(desc=0xAD928, x=MAF, y=MAF_alt)  ; 2D via 0xBE8E4
    I_gain_A = interp_1D(desc=0xACEC8, input=RPM)
    I_gain_B = interp_1D(desc=0xACEDC, input=load_var)
    I_norm   = interp_1D(desc=0xAC510, input=CL_state)

    integral = (I_comp + I_gain_A + I_gain_B) * I_norm

    ; ── STORE INTERMEDIATES ──
    [FFFF7804] = proportional     ; @(base-108)
    [FFFF7808] = integral         ; @(base-104)

    ; ── CONDITIONAL BLENDING ──
    blend_flag = byte[FFFF7871]
    if (blend_flag != 0) → secondary path at 0x34228
    if (flag_B == 1 && CL_state > 4.0) {
        ; Special high-CL-state path
        [FFFF780C] = FPUL
        → blend
    }
    ; Normal blend path continues...

  TABLE DESCRIPTORS AND CURRENT VALUES:

    0xACEA0: P_gain_A — 16 elements, axis = ECT (-40 to 110°C)
             Data: 0.0 below 30°C, ramps 0.5→1.2 from 40→110°C
             Purpose: Suppress P gain when engine is cold

    0xACEB4: P_gain_B — 11 elements, axis = load (0.5 to 1.5)
             Data: ALL ZERO in this ROM
             Purpose: Load-dependent P gain (unused/factory reserved)

    0xAC4FC: P_norm — 11 elements, axis = RPM (0 to 10000)
             Data: 0 below 3000, then 1000→7000 from 4000→10000
             Purpose: RPM-dependent P scaling (high RPM only)
             NOTE: Large values suggest this is a numerator, divided later

    0xACEC8: I_gain_A — 16 elements, axis = ECT (-40 to 110°C)
             Data: flat value across range
             Purpose: ECT-dependent I gain component

    0xACEDC: I_gain_B — 11 elements, axis = load (0.5 to 1.5)
             Data: 0→0.125 ramp above load=1.1
             Purpose: Load-dependent I gain (small corrections at high load)

    0xAC510: I_norm — 11 elements, axis = RPM (0 to 10000)
             Data: 0 below 3000, peak 0.15625 at 8000, 0 above 9000
             Purpose: RPM-dependent I scaling, active only mid-range RPM

    0xAD928: I_comp — 2D table (11 cols × 10 rows)
             Axes: lambda (0.2→1.4) × RPM (800→5000)
             Purpose: Base integral compensation vs lambda and RPM
             NOTE: Table data appears mostly zero — I gain is small

  IMPORTANT: The P_gain tables use the same axis as ECT (-40 to 110°C)
  but the code passes RPM in FR4. The interpolation function at 0xBE830
  clamps out-of-range inputs, so at any RPM > 110 (which is always),
  these tables return their last element value. This means P_gain_A is
  effectively a constant 1.2 during normal operation. The ECT axis only
  matters during very low RPM cranking scenarios (<110 RPM).

─── 0x3439E: afc_enable_gate ──────────────────────────────────────────────

  PSEUDOCODE:
    if (param_2 == 0) {
        result = utility_check_A(0x2BE2C)
    } else {
        result = utility_check_B(0x2BE38)
    }
    if (result != 1) {
        ; Gate CLOSED — load disable value
        output = float[CC010]    ; = 0.0 (AFC zeroed)
    } else {
        ; Gate OPEN — pass through FPUL
        output = FPUL
    }
    [param_1] = output           ; write to caller's destination
    return

  When the enable gate returns 0.0, all AFC correction is disabled.
  The two utility functions at 0x2BE2C/0x2BE38 check engine state
  conditions to determine if CL fuel control is safe to run.

─── 0x343CE: afc_output_clamp ─────────────────────────────────────────────

  GBR = 0xFFFF7820            ; AFC output base

  PSEUDOCODE:
    afc_raw = float[FFFF64D8]  ; unclamped AFC value
    flag_A = word[FFFF79C2]
    flag_B = word[FFFF79C4]

    upper_limit = float[CC014]  ; = 200.0%
    if (afc_raw > upper_limit) {
        byte[GBR+0x52] = 1     ; FFFF7872 = clamp flag set
    } else {
        lower_limit = float[CC018]  ; = 190.0%
        if (afc_raw > lower_limit) {
            ; Between 190-200%: no clamp flag change
        } else {
            byte[GBR+0x52] = 0      ; FFFF7872 = clamp flag clear
        }
    }
    ; Continue with clamped output...

  NOTE: The 190/200 values (CC014/CC018) create a hysteresis band for
  the clamp flag. AFC must exceed 200% to trigger clamping, but won't
  clear the clamp until it drops below 190%. This prevents oscillation
  at the clamp boundary.

─── 0x340A0: BLEND LOGIC (0x34160-0x342A6) — FULL DECOMPILATION ────────────

  After computing proportional (FFFF7804) and integral (FFFF7808),
  the function blends them using a conditional alpha factor.

  R11 = 0xFFFF7870 (workspace base)
  Workspace map:
    FFFF7804  (base-108)  proportional = (P_gain_A + P_gain_B) * P_norm
    FFFF7808  (base-104)  integral = (I_comp + I_gain_A + I_gain_B) * I_norm
    FFFF780C  (base-100)  alpha (blend factor)
    FFFF7810  (base-96)   final P output = proportional * alpha
    FFFF7838  (base-56)   P_gain_A raw lookup
    FFFF783C  (base-52)   P_gain_B raw lookup
    FFFF7840  (base-48)   P_norm raw lookup
    FFFF7844  (base-44)   I_comp raw lookup
    FFFF7848  (base-40)   I_gain_A raw lookup
    FFFF784C  (base-36)   I_gain_B raw lookup
    FFFF7850  (base-32)   I_norm raw lookup
    FFFF7871  (base+1)    blend state flag (byte)

  PSEUDOCODE:

    blend_flag = byte[FFFF7871]    ; saved from previous cycle
    flag_B = byte[FFFF85D7]        ; secondary enable flag
    CL_state = float[FFFF65FC]     ; CL state variable (from stack)

    if (blend_flag != 0) goto SECONDARY_PATH

    ; ── PRIMARY PATH (blend_flag == 0, first cycle) ──
    if (flag_B == 1 && CL_state > 4.0) {
        alpha = FPUL                 ; special high-CL-state alpha
    } else {
        alpha = FPUL                 ; default alpha
    }
    [FFFF780C] = alpha
    goto FINAL_BLEND

  SECONDARY_PATH:    ; blend_flag != 0 (subsequent cycles)
    if (flag_B == 1 && CL_state > 4.0) {
        ; High CL state: lean-adjust alpha
        alpha = [FFFF780C]           ; load current alpha
        alpha = alpha + 10.0         ; add CBFF8 (=10.0)
        alpha = interp_BE970(alpha)  ; lean interpolation
        [FFFF780C] = alpha
    } else {
        ; Default: rich-adjust alpha
        alpha = [FFFF780C]           ; load current alpha
        alpha = alpha - 10.0         ; subtract CBFFC (=10.0)
        alpha = interp_BE960(alpha)  ; rich interpolation
        [FFFF780C] = alpha
    }

  FINAL_BLEND:  ; at 0x34262
    P_output = proportional * alpha           ; FFFF7804 * FFFF780C
    [FFFF7810] = P_output                     ; store final P output
    FPUL = integral                           ; pass I through FPUL to caller
    byte[FFFF7871] = flag_A                   ; save state for next cycle

  DISABLED PATH:  ; at 0x3427E (when flag_A at FFFF8E7E != 1)
    [FFFF7810] = FPUL     ; zero/freeze P output
    [FFFF7804] = FPUL     ; zero proportional
    [FFFF7808] = FPUL     ; zero integral
    byte[FFFF7871] = flag_A
    return

  ADDITIONAL ROM CONSTANTS:
    CBFF4 = 4.0      CL state threshold for high-state path
    CBFF8 = 10.0     Lean alpha adjustment (additive before interp)
    CBFFC = 10.0     Rich alpha adjustment (subtractive before interp)

  KEY INSIGHTS:
  - The blend is NOT a simple alpha*(P) + (1-alpha)*I mix
  - Proportional output is scaled by alpha: P_output = P * alpha
  - Integral is passed through FPUL to the calling function (0x342A8)
  - Alpha evolves over cycles: starts from FPUL, then is adjusted by
    +/-10.0 and re-interpolated each cycle through 0xBE960/0xBE970
  - When CL state (FFFF65FC) exceeds 4.0, the lean interp path is used;
    otherwise the rich interp path applies
  - The blend_flag at FFFF7871 differentiates first-cycle (initialize
    alpha from FPUL) vs subsequent cycles (evolve alpha via interp)

─── AFC PI SYSTEM FLOW SUMMARY ────────────────────────────────────────────

  1. afc_pi_output_stage (0x340A0):
     a) Compute P and I GAIN COEFFICIENTS from 7 table lookups
        → proportional = (P_gain_A + P_gain_B) × P_norm
        → integral = (I_comp + I_gain_A + I_gain_B) × I_norm
     b) Evolve blend alpha:
        → First cycle: alpha = FPUL
        → Subsequent: alpha ±= 10.0, re-interpolated via 0xBE960/0xBE970
     c) Compute final output:
        → P_output = proportional × alpha (stored FFFF7810)
        → I passed through FPUL to caller

  2. afc_pi_controller (0x342A8):
     Compute ERROR and apply state machine
     → error = O2_sensor - current_correction
     → P_output = table_lookup(error)
     → state machine: clamp, step rich/lean by ±1.0, or freeze

  3. afc_enable_gate (0x3439E):
     Gate the output based on engine readiness conditions

  4. afc_output_clamp (0x343CE):
     Clamp final AFC to 190-200% range with hysteresis

  5. Result stored at FFFF77C8 (consumed by fuel correction at 0x320AE)

  AFC CALIBRATION CONSTANTS:
    CC000 = 2.0     P-gain threshold (if lookup > 2.0, use raw value)
    CC004 = 20.0    Max AFC correction (%)
    CC008 = 0.0     Min AFC / dead band
    CC00C = 1.0     Rich/lean step size
    CC010 = 0.0     Enable gate threshold (0 = gates to zero when disabled)
    CC014 = 200.0   Upper clamp limit (%)
    CC018 = 190.0   Lower clamp hysteresis (%)
    CC01C = 0.0     Reserved
    CBFF4 = 4.0     CL state threshold for blend path selection
    CBFF8 = 10.0    Lean alpha step (+10.0 before interp)
    CBFFC = 10.0    Rich alpha step (-10.0 before interp)

  INTERPOLATION FUNCTIONS USED:
    0xBE830  — 1D table interpolation (P and I gain lookups)
    0xBE8E4  — 2D table interpolation (I_comp 2D lookup)
    0xBE960  — Rich-direction interpolation (alpha adjustment)
    0xBE970  — Lean-direction interpolation (alpha adjustment)
    0xBEAB0  — Error-to-correction lookup (P controller in 0x342A8)


================================================================================
SECTION 11: FINAL FUEL CORRECTION ACCUMULATOR (0x320AE)
================================================================================

  This function combines ALL correction factors into the final IPW
  multiplier. It processes a 42-element correction array, applying
  different correction modes to each element.

─── 0x320AE: fuel_correction_final ────────────────────────────────────────

  PARAMETERS (passed via struct pointers):
    R4/R9 = context struct pointer (output destination at [R9])
    R5 = input descriptor struct (correction values)
    R6 = base value descriptor struct

  INPUTS LOADED:
    FR15 = [R6+8]   → base_value_A (e.g., base IPW)
    FR12 = [R6+12]  → base_value_B (e.g., AFC correction FFFF77C8)
    FR4  = [R5+20]  → correction_A (e.g., FFFF77D8)
    FR7  = [R5+24]  → correction_B (e.g., FFFF781C)
    FR2  = [R5+8]   → correction_C (e.g., FFFF77E4)
    FR9  = [R5+4]   → correction_D (e.g., FFFF77DC)

  INITIAL COMPUTATION:
    sum = correction_A + correction_B
    range_result = deadband_check(sum, FPUL, GBR_value)  ; via 0xBE608
    if (range_result != 0) {
        ; Within deadband — compute normalized result
        result = (base_A + base_B + FPUL) / sum
        [output] = result
    }

  LOOP SETUP:
    intermediate values derived from corrections:
      FR14 = 1.0 - base_A - correction_D      ; residual after base and D
      FR15 = correction_D + FPUL               ; D + current value
      FR13 = correction_D - base_B             ; D - B delta
      FR12 = FPUL (re-assigned)
    loop_count = 42                              ; R8 = 42
    element_index = 1                            ; R14 starts at 1
    stride = 4 bytes (float)                     ; R13 increments by 4

  CORRECTION LOOP (42 iterations):
    For each element i (1 to 42):
      output_array = [R9+16]                     ; output array base

      switch (correction_mode):
        case 1:   ; DIRECT COPY
          output_array[i] = FR14                 ; write residual directly

        case 2:   ; THRESHOLD COMPARE
          if (correction_C > threshold) {
              output_array[i] = FR13 (delta)     ; D-B delta
              FPUL = FR15                        ; update accumulator
          } else {
              goto DEFAULT                       ; fall through to default
          }

        case (i > remaining_count):
          if (i > 1) {
              ; MULTIPLY + ACCUMULATE
              temp = output_array[i-1] * FR12    ; prev * factor
              prev_val = output_array[i-2]       ; load 2-back
              FPUL = FR15
              output_array[i] = temp             ; store
          } else if (i == 2) {
              goto DEFAULT
          } else {
              ; DIRECT FPUL STORE
              output_array[i] = FPUL
          }

        default:  ; FULL CORRECTION CALC (via bsr 0x32892)
          output_array[i] = correction_calc(
              R4=context, FR4=stack[0], FR5=stack[12],
              FR6=stack[0], FR7=stack[4])

      element_index++
      stride advances by 4

  The sub-function at 0x32892 performs the per-element correction
  calculation, reading from the context struct and applying individual
  compensation factors.

  KEY INSIGHT: The 42-element array corresponds to the per-cylinder
  and per-condition correction factors. Each element can be:
  - Directly set (mode 1)
  - Threshold-gated (mode 2)
  - Multiplied from previous elements
  - Fully calculated via the sub-function

  The final output at [R9] contains the combined correction multiplier
  that scales base IPW into the final injector pulse width.


================================================================================
SECTION 12: GENERIC TABLE PROCESSORS (0xBE5A8-0xBEAB0)
================================================================================

  The ROM uses a unified table lookup system with descriptor-driven
  dispatch. All interpolation is routed through these common functions.

─── TABLE DESCRIPTOR FORMAT (20 bytes) ────────────────────────────────────

  For 1D tables:
    Byte 0:    0x00 (1D indicator)
    Byte 1:    Element count (N)
    Byte 2:    Data type selector (dispatches to reader function)
               0x04 = float32 data (4 bytes per element)
               0x08 = alternate format (possibly uint16 scaled)
    Byte 3:    0x00
    Byte 4-7:  Axis pointer (ROM address, N floats)
    Byte 8-11: Data pointer (ROM address, N elements)
    Byte 12-15: Default low value (float, returned when type==0)
    Byte 16-19: Default high value (float)

  For 2D tables:
    Byte 0:    0x00
    Byte 1:    Column count
    Byte 2:    0x00
    Byte 3:    Row count
    Byte 4-7:  Row axis pointer (ROM address)
    Byte 8-11: Column axis pointer (ROM address)
    Byte 12-15: Data pointer (ROM address, rows*cols elements)
    Byte 16-19: Type/flags

  EXAMPLES FROM THIS ROM:
    0xACEA0: 00 10 08 00 ... → 1D, 16 elements, type 0x08
    0xAC4FC: 00 0B 04 00 ... → 1D, 11 elements, type 0x04 (float32)
    0xAD928: 00 0B 00 0A ... → 2D, 11 cols × 10 rows

─── FUNCTION CATALOG ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────

  0xBE5A8: axis_position_calc_u8
    Computes fractional position of input within axis range.
    Clamps result to 0..255 (uint8).
    formula: index = (input - axis[i]) / (axis[i+1] - axis[i]) + offset
    Returns clamped integer index in R0.

  0xBE5D8: axis_position_calc_u16
    Same as 0xBE5A8 but clamps to 0..65535 (uint16).

  0xBE608: deadband_check
    Returns 1 if input is within tolerance band of target.
    PSEUDOCODE:
      lower = target - tolerance       ; FR5 - FR6
      upper = target + tolerance       ; FR5 + FR6
      if (input > lower && input < upper)
          return 1    ; within deadband
      else
          return 0    ; outside deadband

  0xBE628: normalize_ratio
    Computes ratio FR4/FR5 with special-case handling.
    PSEUDOCODE:
      if (FR5 == FPUL) {
          return FR4 / FR5              ; normal division
      } else if (FR4 == FPUL) {
          return FPUL                   ; identity
      } else {
          ; edge case: load from GBR-relative table
          if (FR4 > FPUL)
              return FPUL               ; clamp
          else
              return loaded_value
      }

  0xBE830: interp_1D (MAIN 1D INTERPOLATOR)
    Primary 1D table interpolation with type dispatch.
    PSEUDOCODE:
      count = word[desc+0]             ; element count
      axis_ptr = [desc+4]             ; axis array
      index = axis_search(input, axis_ptr, count)  ; bsr 0xBECA8
      data_type = byte[desc+2]        ; type selector
      reader_func = dispatch_table[data_type]  ; via GBR vtable
      result = reader_func(index, [desc+8])    ; read+interpolate data
      if (data_type == 0) {
          ; No data type → use defaults
          FR0 = float[desc+12]         ; default low
          FR1 = float[desc+16]         ; default high
          FPUL = interpolated
      }
      return FR0

  0xBE874: interp_1D_variant
    Variant of 0xBE830 that calls a different data reader (0xBEB20).
    Used for uint8-scaled data (extu.b result at end).

  0xBE890: interp_1D_2input
    1D interpolation with two inputs (FR4=primary, FR5=secondary).
    Uses axis search variant at 0xBECDC that takes two values.
    Data reader at 0xBEB40.

  0xBE8AC: interp_1D_u16
    1D interpolation returning uint16 result (extu.w at end).

  0xBE8E4: interp_2D (MAIN 2D INTERPOLATOR)
    2D table interpolation.
    PSEUDOCODE:
      bsr 0xBED98                     ; 2D axis search (both dims)
      row_type = byte[desc+16]        ; data type
      reader_func = dispatch[row_type]
      result = reader_func(indices, [desc+12])  ; read+interp 2D data
      if (row_type == 0) {
          FR0 = float[desc+20]
          FR1 = float[desc+24]        ; defaults
      }
      return FR0

  0xBE960: clamp_min (RICH DIRECTION)
    Returns min(FR4, FR5).
    PSEUDOCODE:
      if (FR5 > FR4): return FR4       ; FR4 is smaller
      else: return FR5                 ; FR5 is smaller

  0xBE970: clamp_max (LEAN DIRECTION)
    Returns max(FR4, FR5).
    PSEUDOCODE:
      if (FR4 > FR5): return FR4       ; FR4 is larger
      else: return FR5                 ; FR5 is larger

  0xBEAB0: subtract
    Simple subtraction: return FR4 - FR5, also stores in FPUL.

  0xBECA8: axis_search (1D)
    Binary/linear search for input value position within sorted axis.
    Walks axis array comparing FR0 against each float element.
    Returns fractional position for interpolation.

  0xBECDC: axis_search_2input
    Axis search variant taking two input values (R2=secondary).
    Used for 2D interpolation first-dimension search.

  0xBED98: axis_search_2D
    Full 2D axis search. Finds position in both row and column axes.

─── DATA TYPE DISPATCH ────────────────────────────────────────────────────

  The byte at descriptor offset 2 selects how data is read:

    Type 0x00: No data — return default floats from bytes 12-19
    Type 0x04: float32 — 4 bytes per element, direct FPU load
    Type 0x08: Alternate — likely fixed-point or scaled integer
               (data pointers at unaligned addresses suggest 2-byte data)

  The dispatch is done via a GBR-relative function pointer table:
    C706 = mov.l @(0x18,GBR),R0 → reader for one type
    C707 = mov.l @(0x1C,GBR),R0 → reader for another type
    C708 = mov.l @(0x20,GBR),R0 → reader for yet another type

  The reader functions at 0xBEACC, 0xBEB00, 0xBEB20 handle the actual
  data loading and delta computation for interpolation.


  REMAINING WORK:

  1. Apply labels via ImportAE5L600L.java Ghidra script

;     0x38D16  ltft_learning_init      — Step-size 0.001, workspace FFFF7B60
;     0x38E30  ltft_learning_calc      — LTFT algorithm, RPM thresh 3600
;
;   Stage 9: Default output
;     0x399EE  fuel_output_default     — Set 1.05 multiplier (5% enrichment)
;
; RAM workspace: FFFF7340 - FFFF7BDC (continuous ~2000 bytes)


; ======================================================================
; FUELING PIPELINE B (0x49CF0) — Parallel Fuel Chain
; Called from main loop at 0xE556
; ======================================================================
;
; Pipeline B handles corrections, per-cylinder trim, and special modes:
;
;   Shared with Pipeline A:
;     0x32AA8  fuel_correction_array_update
;     0x31C9C  fuel_cyl_arrays_init
;     0x32958  fuel_corr_filter_init
;
;   Unique to Pipeline B:
;     0x332A2  fuel_main_entry           — Main fueling entry
;     0x31528  fuel_enable_state_update   — Sensor validity -> FFFF744B
;     0x3160A  fuel_correction_calc       — Major correction aggregator
;     0x31A4C  fuel_trim_init             — Fuel trim init, gear-dep cal IDs
;     0x30ACC  fuel_base_map_combine      — Dual 2D map combiner -> FFFF73AC
;     0x3452A  afl_core_entry             — A/F Learning core
;     0x34EF4  clol_conditions_calc_B     — CL/OL conditions (entry B)
;     0x3580C  clol_transition_core       — CL/OL transition core
;     0x3605E  ol_fuel_map_selector       — OL map: IAM vs 0.5 threshold
;     0x36C3C  clol_state_cleanup         — CL/OL state cleanup
;     0x37186  fuel_transient_comp        — Transient fuel (tip-in/out)
;     0x37B68  fuel_injector_comp         — Injector compensation maps
;     0x39528  fuel_wot_enrich_calc       — WOT enrichment factor
;     0x3A222  fuel_per_cyl_trim          — Per-cylinder trim (4-cyl loop)
;     0x3BB6C  fuel_accel_enrich          — Acceleration enrichment
;     0x3CD34  fuel_warmup_enrich         — Warmup/cold-start enrichment
;     0x3EB8C  fuel_overrun_cutoff        — Deceleration fuel cut
;
;   Also calls (non-fuel subsystems from Pipeline B):
;     0x403C4  ect_warmup_timing_corr  — ECT warmup timing correction (4 mode-selected curves → FFFF7F68)
;     0x419CC  - (timing related)
;     0x4FD5E  - (boost control)
;     0x4F368  - (boost control)
;     0x4F206  - (boost control)
;     0x56AAA  - (emissions)
;     0x5CE9C  - (auxiliary)
;     0x5AB44  - (auxiliary)
;     0x5F87A  - (auxiliary)
;     ... and ~30 more diagnostic/peripheral functions


; ======================================================================
; ADC / SENSOR INPUT PIPELINE
; ======================================================================
;
; This section documents the complete analog sensor input chain:
;   Hardware ADC registers -> ISR -> GBR-relative RAM -> sensor variables
;
; ── SH7058 ADC Hardware ──────────────────────────────────────────────
;
; The SH7058 has three independent A/D converter groups, each with its
; own control/status register and set of data channels.  The ADC is a
; 10-bit successive approximation converter.
;
; ADC Peripheral Register Map (from SH7055/SH7058 Hardware Manual):
;
;   Group 0 Data Registers:
;     0xFFFFF800: ADDR0H/L    0xFFFFF802: ADDR1H/L
;     0xFFFFF804: ADDR2H/L    0xFFFFF806: ADDR3H/L
;     0xFFFFF808: ADDR4H/L    0xFFFFF80A: ADDR5H/L
;     0xFFFFF80C: ADDR6H/L    0xFFFFF80E: ADDR7H/L
;     0xFFFFF810: ADDR8H/L    0xFFFFF812: ADDR9H/L
;     0xFFFFF814: ADDR10H/L   0xFFFFF816: ADDR11H/L
;     0xFFFFF818: ADCSR0      (A/D Control/Status Register 0)
;     0xFFFFF819: ADCR0       (A/D Control Register 0)
;
;   Group 1 Data Registers:
;     0xFFFFF820: ADDR12H/L   0xFFFFF822: ADDR13H/L
;     0xFFFFF824: ADDR14H/L   0xFFFFF826: ADDR15H/L
;     0xFFFFF828: ADDR16H/L   0xFFFFF82A: ADDR17H/L
;     0xFFFFF82C: ADDR18H/L   0xFFFFF82E: ADDR19H/L
;     0xFFFFF830: ADDR20H/L   0xFFFFF832: ADDR21H/L
;     0xFFFFF834: ADDR22H/L   0xFFFFF836: ADDR23H/L
;     0xFFFFF838: ADCSR1      (A/D Control/Status Register 1)
;     0xFFFFF839: ADCR1       (A/D Control Register 1)
;
;   Group 2 Data Registers:
;     0xFFFFF840: ADDR24H/L   0xFFFFF842: ADDR25H/L
;     0xFFFFF844: ADDR26H/L   0xFFFFF846: ADDR27H/L
;     0xFFFFF848: ADDR28H/L   0xFFFFF84A: ADDR29H/L
;     0xFFFFF84C: ADDR30H/L   0xFFFFF84E: ADDR31H/L
;     0xFFFFF858: ADCSR2      (A/D Control/Status Register 2)
;     0xFFFFF859: ADCR2       (A/D Control Register 2)
;
;   ADC Trigger Registers:
;     0xFFFFF72E: ADTRGR1     0xFFFFF72F: ADTRGR2
;     0xFFFFF76E: ADTRG0
;
; ADCSR Bit Layout:
;   Bit 7: ADF  - A/D End Flag (1 = conversion complete, poll this)
;   Bit 6: ADIE - A/D Interrupt Enable
;   Bit 5: ADST - A/D Start (write 1 to begin conversion)
;   Bits 4-3: Scan mode select
;   Bits 2-0: Channel group select
;
; ADCR Bit Layout:
;   Bit 5: TRGE - External trigger enable
;   Bits 1-0: CKS - Clock select (conversion speed)
;
; ── Peripheral Interrupt Vector Table ────────────────────────────────
;
; VBR (Vector Base Register) = 0x000FFC50  (set at 0x0FA40)
;
; At boot, VBR=0 (vectors 0-13 at ROM 0x000-0x037).  During init,
; VBR is changed to 0x000FFC50, relocating the peripheral interrupt
; vector table to ROM offset 0xFFC50.
;
; Key peripheral interrupt vectors (VBR + vec*4):
;
;   Vec  64 IRQ0             -> 0x207C -> 0xE8D8   (external interrupt 0)
;   Vec  65 IRQ1             -> 0x2094 -> 0xE8E4
;   Vec  66 IRQ2             -> 0x20AC -> 0xE8F0
;   Vec  67 IRQ3             -> 0x20C4 -> 0xE8FC
;   Vec  68 IRQ4             -> 0x20DC -> 0xE908
;   Vec  69 IRQ5             -> 0x20F4 -> 0xE914
;   Vec  70 IRQ6             -> 0x210C -> 0xE920
;   Vec  71 IRQ7             -> 0x2124 -> 0xE92C
;   Vec  80 ATU_ITV          -> 0x219C -> 0xE970   (interval timer - scheduler tick)
;   Vec 172 CMT_CMI0         -> 0x27E4 -> 0xF2F6   (compare match timer 0)
;   Vec 176 ADI0             -> 0x2814 -> 0xF312   (A/D Group 0 conversion complete)
;   Vec 177 ADI1             -> 0xE852              (shared handler - halt on error)
;   Vec 204 WDT_ITI          -> 0x2904              (watchdog timer)
;
; All ISR stubs use a common pattern:
;   push r0, r1, pr
;   jsr  0x2B8C            ; ISR common dispatcher (saves full FPU context)
;   load r1 = handler_addr
;   jsr  @r2               ; call actual handler (r2 set by dispatcher)
;
; ISR Common Dispatcher @ 0x2B8C:
;   - Saves r2-r7, fr0-fr11, FPSCR, mach, macl to stack
;   - Reads interrupt nesting counter from 0xFFFF1288+8
;   - Restores SR from context, increments nesting count
;   - Returns to stub with r0 = 0x2BD4 (epilogue address)
;   - Epilogue at 0x2BD4 restores all registers, decrements nesting count
;
; ── ADC Bulk Read Function @ 0x040E0 ────────────────────────────────
;
; This is the main ADC acquisition routine.  It configures all three
; ADC groups, starts simultaneous conversions, polls for completion,
; then bulk-copies all results to GBR-relative RAM.
;
; Called from the scheduler (not from ADI0 ISR).  Runs synchronously:
; starts conversion, spins until all 3 groups finish, then reads.
;
; Phase 1: Configure ADC Groups (0x040E0-0x0415A)
;
;   r12 = 0xFFFFF818 (ADCSR0)  - loaded from literal pool @0x0424A
;   r11 = 0xFFFFF838 (ADCSR1)  - loaded from literal pool @0x0424C
;   r14 = 0xFFFFF858 (ADCSR2)  - loaded from literal pool @0x0424E
;
;   For each group:
;     1. Clear ADCR bit 5 (disable trigger)
;     2. Write channel select to ADCSR:
;        - Group 0: 0x33 = scan AN0-AN3, multi-mode
;        - Group 1: 0x33 = scan AN12-AN15, multi-mode
;        - Group 2: 0x2B = scan AN24-AN27, single-scan
;     3. Set ADCR bit 5 (enable), set scan mode bits
;     4. Call setup function (0xBE81C or 0xBE82C)
;
; Phase 2: Start and Poll (0x0415A-0x04176)
;
;   0x0415C: GBR+128 = 2   (ADC state: "converting")
;   0x04160: GBR+133 = 0   (clear result flag)
;   0x04164: GBR+134 = 0xFF (set "all groups pending" mask)
;
;   Poll loop (0x04166-0x04176):
;     while (ADCSR0.ADF == 0) spin;  // @r12 bit 7
;     while (ADCSR1.ADF == 0) spin;  // @r11 bit 7
;     while (ADCSR2.ADF == 0) spin;  // @r14 bit 7
;
; Phase 3: Bulk Read Group 0 (0x04178-0x041AC)
;
;   r14 = 0xFFFFF800 (ADDR0 base)
;
;   ADDR0  -> GBR+0     ADDR1  -> GBR+2     ADDR2  -> GBR+4
;   ADDR3  -> GBR+6     ADDR4  -> GBR+8     ADDR5  -> GBR+10
;   ADDR6  -> GBR+12    ADDR7  -> GBR+14    ADDR8  -> GBR+16
;   ADDR9  -> GBR+18    ADDR10 -> GBR+20    ADDR11 -> GBR+22
;
; Phase 4: Bulk Read Group 1 (0x041AE-0x041DC)
;
;   r12 = 0xFFFFF820 (ADDR12 base, from earlier config)
;   Reads @(8,r12) through @(30,r12) -> GBR+24 through GBR+46
;   This corresponds to ADDR16-ADDR23 (channels 16-23)
;
; Phase 5: Bulk Read Group 2 (0x041DE+)
;
;   r11 = 0xFFFFF838 region -> reads remaining channels
;   Stores to GBR+48+
;
; The GBR value during this function determines which RAM struct
; receives the raw ADC data.  This is set by the calling context
; (scheduler task).
;
; ── Knock ADC Snapshot @ 0x0437C ────────────────────────────────────
;
; Called during knock detection to re-read all ADC channels and store
; them in a dedicated knock detection RAM struct.
;
; Group 0 Read (0x0437C-0x043C6):
;   r6 = 0xFFFFF800 (ADDR0 base, via mov #-8,r6; shll8 r6)
;   r5 = 0xFFFF4064 (destination struct, from literal pool @0x04628)
;
;   Reads ADDR11 downto ADDR0 and stores to 0xFFFF4064+offset:
;     ADDR0  -> 0xFFFF4064    ADDR1  -> 0xFFFF4066
;     ADDR2  -> 0xFFFF4068    ADDR3  -> 0xFFFF406A
;     ADDR4  -> 0xFFFF406C    ADDR5  -> 0xFFFF406E
;     ADDR6  -> 0xFFFF4070    ADDR7  -> 0xFFFF4072
;     ADDR8  -> 0xFFFF4074    ADDR9  -> 0xFFFF4076
;     ADDR10 -> 0xFFFF4078    ADDR11 -> 0xFFFF407A
;
; Group 1 Read (0x04410-0x04450):
;   Dispatch by cylinder count byte @(0xFFFF40AD):
;     12 -> read Group 1 (ADDR12-ADDR23) to 0xFFFF407C
;      8 -> read channels 16-23
;      4 -> read channels 20-23
;      1 -> read channel 23 only
;
;   r6 = 0xFFFFF820 (ADDR12 base, via mov.w literal 0xF820 sign-extended)
;   r5 = 0xFFFF407C (destination, from literal pool @0x04638)
;
;   Full Group 1:
;     ADDR12 -> 0xFFFF407C    ADDR13 -> 0xFFFF407E
;     ADDR14 -> 0xFFFF4080    ADDR15 -> 0xFFFF4082
;     ADDR16 -> 0xFFFF4084    ADDR17 -> 0xFFFF4086
;     ADDR18 -> 0xFFFF4088    ADDR19 -> 0xFFFF408A
;     ADDR20 -> 0xFFFF408C    ADDR21 -> 0xFFFF408E
;     ADDR22 -> 0xFFFF4090    ADDR23 -> 0xFFFF4092
;
; ── ADI0 Interrupt Handler @ 0xF312 ─────────────────────────────────
;
; The ADI0 ISR (A/D Group 0 conversion complete) is invoked via:
;   Vector 176 -> stub at 0x2814 -> dispatcher 0x2B8C -> handler 0xF312
;
; Handler at 0xF312:
;   1. Reads ADCSR0 status from 0xFFFFF6E8 (sign-extended 0xF6E8)
;   2. Writes 14 (0x0E) to ADCSR0 -> clears ADF flag, sets next scan mode
;   3. Calls ADC state machine dispatcher at 0xE774 with state code 0x00B0
;
; Second handler at 0xF320 (also called from ADI0 vector):
;   1. Reads ADCSR0 status, writes 11 (0x0B) -> next state
;   2. Calls three functions sequentially:
;      - 0x7110: ADC data copy/processing
;      - 0x7D26: sensor scaling/conversion
;      - 0xBB6C: notification/flag setting
;
; The ADI0 path manages the ADC state machine that cycles through
; different scan groups and conversion modes.  The actual sensor data
; is read in the bulk read function (0x040E0), not in the ISR.
;
; ── Peripheral Access Summary ────────────────────────────────────────
;
; All peripheral register accesses in this ROM use the SH-2 pattern:
;   mov  #imm, Rn    ; load sign-extended 8-bit immediate
;   shll8 Rn         ; shift left 8 -> creates 0xFFFFxx00 base address
;
; Peripheral access locations by base address:
;
;   0xFFFFF000 (SCI - Serial Communication Interface):
;     0x5A93E, 0x5A988
;
;   0xFFFFF700 (APC/CMT/IO/ADC Trigger Control):
;     0x00058, 0x01014
;
;   0xFFFFF800 (ADC Data Registers):
;     0x04178, 0x0437C, 0x04392, 0x043A8, 0x043BA
;
; INTC (Interrupt Controller) Registers:
;   0xFFFFED00: IPRA   0xFFFFED02: IPRB   0xFFFFED04: IPRC
;   0xFFFFED06: IPRD   0xFFFFED08: IPRE   0xFFFFED0A: IPRF
;   0xFFFFED0C: IPRG   0xFFFFED0E: IPRH   0xFFFFED10: IPRI
;   0xFFFFED12: IPRJ   0xFFFFED14: IPRK   0xFFFFED16: IPRL
;   0xFFFFED18: ICR    0xFFFFED1A: ISR
;
; ── ADC RAM Structures ───────────────────────────────────────────────
;
; Primary ADC results (via bulk read to GBR-relative offsets):
;   GBR+0x00 through GBR+0x16: Group 0 raw ADC (ADDR0-ADDR11), 16-bit each
;   GBR+0x18 through GBR+0x2E: Group 1 raw ADC, 16-bit each
;   GBR+0x30+:                 Group 2 raw ADC, 16-bit each
;   GBR+0x80:                  ADC state byte (2=converting)
;   GBR+0x85:                  Result ready flag
;   GBR+0x86:                  Groups pending mask (0xFF=all pending)
;
; Knock ADC snapshot (fixed addresses, not GBR-relative):
;   0xFFFF4064-0xFFFF407A: Group 0 raw ADC snapshot (12 channels x 2 bytes)
;   0xFFFF407C-0xFFFF4092: Group 1 raw ADC snapshot (12 channels x 2 bytes)
;   0xFFFF40AB:            Cylinder count dispatch byte
;
; ISR context block:
;   0xFFFF1288:            ISR nesting context struct
;   0xFFFF1288+8:          Interrupt nesting counter
;   0xFFFF1288+16:         Saved SR for interrupt priority
;
; ── Key Functions ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
;
;   0x00002B8C  ISR_CommonDispatcher   - saves full FPU context for ISRs
;   0x00002BD4  ISR_CommonEpilogue     - restores context, manages nesting
;   0x000040E0  ADC_BulkRead           - synchronous read of all 32 ADC channels
;   0x0000F312  ADI0_Handler           - ADC Group 0 conversion complete handler
;   0x0000F320  ADI0_Handler2          - ADC state machine + sensor processing
;   0x0000E774  ADC_StateMachine       - ADC conversion state dispatcher
;   0x0000E852  ISR_SharedHalt         - shared error/unused interrupt handler
;   0x00007110  ADC_DataCopy           - copy ADC results to working RAM
;   0x00007D26  Sensor_Scaling         - raw ADC -> engineering units conversion
;   0x0000BB6C  ADC_Notify             - set flags after ADC processing complete
;
; ── ADC Float Conversion Stats ───────────────────────────────────────
;
;   Total 'float FPUL,FRn' instructions in ROM: 192
;   Total 'lds Rm,FPUL; float FPUL,FRn' (int->float) pairs: 135
;   These represent points where raw integer ADC values are converted
;   to IEEE 754 single-precision floats for use in the fuel, timing,
;   and knock control algorithms.


; ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
; End of disassembly  |  ROM: AE5L600L rev 20.2  |  1,048,576 bytes
; Arch: SH-2 BE  |  Ghidra 12.0.2  |  SuperH:BE:32:SH-2:default
; ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
================================================================================
  AFL PERSISTENCE AND CL/OL TRANSITION DELAY ANALYSIS
  Subaru ECU ROM AE5L600L (SH7055 / SH-2)
  Stock ROM: ae5l600l.bin
  Modified ROM: AE5L600L 20g rev 20.5 tiny wrex.bin
  Date: 2026-03-26
================================================================================

PROBLEM STATEMENT

  Despite CL-to-OL delay being set to 0 (CBC62=0), datalogs show:
    1. A significant delay before OL behavior fully engages
    2. AFC drops immediately on CL->OL transition (correct)
    3. AFL lingers well into what should be OL operation
    4. AFL persists past its max g/s boundary of 40.0 (CC07C)
    5. The lingering AFL causes a lean condition during OL

  This analysis traces the complete AFL and CL/OL transition codepath
  to identify the root causes.


================================================================================
SECTION 1: THE TWO INDEPENDENT CL/OL PATHS
================================================================================

  CRITICAL FINDING: There are TWO completely separate mechanisms that
  determine CL/OL behavior in this ECU. They operate independently and
  can be out of sync:

  PATH A — OL Enrichment State Machine (7-Phase Pipeline):
    Controls: OL fuel enrichment computation
    Delay control: counter_B at FFFF79C4, set by CBC62 (modified=0)
    When delay=0: OL enrichment is computed immediately
    Flags written: FFFF79F2 (OL active), FFFF79C6 (mode state, always 0)

  PATH B — CL/OL Mode Flag (FFFF7448):
    Controls: AFC feedback (PI controller at 0x342A8) and AFL learning
    Writer: Single function at ROM 0x031528
    Called from: Task scheduler dispatch at 0x049EA4
    Inputs: FFFF8E98 -> FFFF744B (inhibit)
            FFFF7452 (master readiness) + FFFF744E (mode) -> FFFF7449/744A
    NO DEPENDENCY on CBC62 delay parameter

  These two paths use DIFFERENT conditions to determine mode. Path A uses
  the condition checker (ol_condition_checker) with throttle/RPM/load thresholds.
  Path B uses a completely different set of flags (FFFF8E98, FFFF7452,
  FFFF744E) derived from sensor processing functions.

  When you set delay=0, you only affect Path A (OL enrichment). Path B
  has its own timing determined by FFFF7452 (master readiness flag) which
  has its own conditions and hysteresis at ROM 0x031966.


================================================================================
SECTION 2: WHY AFC DROPS IMMEDIATELY BUT AFL LINGERS
================================================================================

  AFC (A/F Correction) — GATED BY FFFF7448:
    The AFC PI controller at 0x342A8 reads FFFF7448 every cycle.
    When FFFF7448 = 0 (OL), AFC correction output = 0.
    AFC drops immediately because FFFF7448 transitions to 0 promptly
    (the FFFF7448 writer at 0x031528 clears it as soon as FFFF744B != 0
    OR the mode conditions fail).

  AFL (A/F Learning) — NOT GATED BY FFFF7448 FOR APPLICATION:

    AFL has TWO separate operations:

    1. AFL LEARNING (value update):
       Function: 0x34884 (afl_value_update)
       Gate: 10-condition check at 0x345A4 (cl_active_check)
       CL/OL check: YES — function at 0x34C54 reads FFFF7448
       When FFFF7448=0: Learning is FROZEN (no updates to stored values)
       This works correctly.

    2. AFL APPLICATION (applying learned values to fueling):
       Function: 0x37B74 (afl_application)
       Multiplier output: FFFF7AB4
       CL/OL check: **NO** — DOES NOT read FFFF7448
       Airflow gate: **NO** — no airflow comparison in application path
       Only gates: FFFF726C (transient flag), FFFF7C68 (status flag)
       When gating fails: writes 1.0 (no correction) to FFFF7AB4
       When gating passes: writes learned AFL multiplier to FFFF7AB4

       The fuel pulse width calculation at 0x0301E4 reads FFFF7AB4
       and applies it unconditionally as a multiplier. There is NO
       CL/OL mode check in the fuel calculation path.

  RESULT: AFL learned values continue to be applied to fueling during
  OL operation. This is by design in the stock ROM — Subaru's OEM logic
  intentionally carries AFL corrections into OL. The base definition
  confirms this: "These are the airflow ranges in which the different
  long-term fuel trims are calculated in closed loop and applied to the
  same airflow ranges for both closed loop and open loop."


================================================================================
SECTION 3: THE 40 G/S BOUNDARY (CC07C) — WHY IT DOESN'T CUT OFF AFL
================================================================================

  Modified ROM AFL airflow ranges (CC074):
    Range A: 6.0 g/s  (stock: 5.6)
    Range B: 23.0 g/s (stock: 10.0)
    Range C: 40.0 g/s (stock: 50.0)  <-- user's "max g/s of 40"

  These values at CC074 define the BREAKPOINTS of the AFL interpolation
  table. They determine which airflow zones the 4 learning values
  (FFFF316C/3174/317C/3184) correspond to. They do NOT define a cutoff.

  How AFL application works:
    1. Current airflow is read
    2. The airflow is located within the range table (which range?)
    3. The learning value for that range is interpolated
    4. The interpolated value is applied as a multiplier

  Above 40.0 g/s: The AFL function uses Range C and Range D values.
  Range D has CC08C=35.0 and CC090=0.0 (disabled). But Range C (at
  FFFF317C) may have a non-zero learned value. If it does, AFL continues
  to apply above 40 g/s.

  THERE IS NO "MAX AIRFLOW" GATE IN THE AFL APPLICATION PATH.

  The "A/F #1 Learning Max Threshold" parameter exists in the 32BITBASE
  definition (for newer ECU architectures), but it is NOT defined and
  NOT present in the AE5L600L ROM. This ECU does not have an airflow-
  based cutoff for AFL application.

  The only way AFL application stops is:
    - FFFF726C (transient flag) is set (rapid airflow change)
    - FFFF7C68 (engine status flag) indicates abnormal condition
    - Both of these bypass AFL and write 1.0 to FFFF7AB4


================================================================================
SECTION 4: THE LEAN CONDITION MECHANISM
================================================================================

  During steady-state CL operation (cruise, light load):
    - O2 sensor feedback drives AFC correction
    - AFL learns long-term trim corrections per airflow range
    - If injectors are over-fueling, AFL learns a NEGATIVE correction
      (pulling fuel to maintain stoich)
    - If injectors are under-fueling, AFL learns a POSITIVE correction

  On CL->OL transition (WOT, boost):
    - AFC drops to 0 immediately (FFFF7448 clears)
    - OL enrichment computation kicks in (Path A, delay=0)
    - OL fuel maps provide the "correct" fuel for high-load operation
    - BUT: AFL correction from CL is STILL applied as a multiplier

  If AFL had learned a NEGATIVE correction (reducing fuel by, say, -5%):
    - OL fuel = OL_map_value * (1.0 + AFL_trim)
    - OL fuel = OL_map_value * (1.0 - 0.05) = OL_map_value * 0.95
    - The fuel is 5% LEANER than the OL map intends
    - This creates the observed lean condition

  The lean persists for the entire OL event because:
    1. AFL learning is frozen (no updates to correct the trim)
    2. AFL application continues with the stale CL-learned value
    3. There is no airflow gate to disable application at high airflow
    4. The AFL value only changes when the ECU returns to CL and
       the learning function updates it over many cycles


================================================================================
SECTION 5: FFFF7448 WRITER — COMPLETE LOGIC
================================================================================

  Single writer: Function at ROM 0x031528
  Called from: Task scheduler at 0x049EA4 (dispatch table 0x04A0D0)

  PHASE 1 — Input collection (0x03152E-0x031546):
    FFFF744B <- FFFF8E98 (primary inhibit sensor flag)
    FFFF744C <- FFFF8F08 (readiness A)
    FFFF744D <- func_021D9A(FFFF8F24) (readiness B)
    FFFF744E <- func_021D9A result (mode: 0, 1, or 2)

  PHASE 2 — Derived flags (0x03154C-0x031558):
    FFFF744A = (FFFF7452==1 AND FFFF744E==1) ? 1 : 0
    FFFF7449 = (FFFF7452==1 AND FFFF744E==2) ? 1 : 0

  PHASE 3 — Final FFFF7448 computation (0x03155C-0x03158E):

    if (FFFF744B != 0):
        FFFF7448 = 0                    // CL inhibited
    else if (FFFF744D==1 AND FFFF744C!=0):
        FFFF7448 = 0                    // Secondary forces OL
    else if (FFFF7449==1 OR FFFF744A==1):
        FFFF7448 = 1                    // ENTER CL
    else:
        FFFF7448 = 0                    // STAY OL

  MASTER READINESS (FFFF7452):
    Written at 0x031966 (GBR=FFFF7450)
    Requires multiple simultaneous conditions:
      - Throttle, load, RPM all within thresholds
      - FFFF7BB0 == 0 (no active fault)
      - Hysteresis logic satisfied
    This has its OWN timing and conditions independent of the CL/OL
    state machine delay parameter.


================================================================================
SECTION 6: FFFF79C6 (MODE STATE FLAG) — ALWAYS ZERO
================================================================================

  FFFF79C6 is NEVER WRITTEN anywhere in the stock ROM.
  It is initialized to 0 by the SH7055 startup RAM clear.

  ol_enrichment_dispatch reads it at 0x0361EC and switches on the value:
    - Value 1 (CL path): copies enrichment directly  -> DEAD CODE
    - Value 2 (blending path): MAC blending          -> DEAD CODE
    - Value 0 (default): normal enrichment path      -> ALWAYS TAKEN

  The mode_state==1 and mode_state==2 paths in ol_enrichment_dispatch are
  unreachable code in the stock and modified ROMs. They appear to be
  hooks for aftermarket ECU patches that could inject mode overrides
  by writing to this RAM address.


================================================================================
SECTION 7: AFL SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE
================================================================================

  DISPATCH TABLE A (0x480B8):
    Entry [5] = 0x34488 — AFL sub-dispatcher
    Entry [7] = 0x34EC8 — AFL airflow processor

  AFL CORE FUNCTION (0x3452A) — Called from sub-dispatcher:
    Step 1: bsr 0x34D52 — Airflow range determination (selects range 0-3)
    Step 2: bsr 0x345A4 — CL active check (10-condition gate)
    Step 3: bsr 0x34778 — Range selection (additional enable logic)
    Step 4: bsr 0x34884 — Value update (actual learning adjustment)
    Step 5: bsr 0x34B1C — Value store (clamp + write to array)
    Step 6: bsr 0x34CC8 — Max airflow check (35 g/s rate boundary)
    Step 7: bsr 0x34C18 — CL/OL transition handler

  CL ACTIVE CHECK (0x345A4) — 10 CONDITIONS:
    1. FFFF8F24 != 0 -> fail (global inhibit)
    2. MAF > 70.0 g/s (CC020) -> fail (max airflow for learning)
    3. FFFF73A4 check (threshold 0.003906)
    4. FFFF7354 check (threshold 0.000244)
    5. FFFF7374 check (threshold 0.000244)
    6. FFFF7A14 check (threshold 0.000977) — transition output, always 0.0
    7. FFFF7A20 check (threshold 0.003906) — blending rate, always 0.1
    8. FFFF7D18 must be 0
    9. FFFF8F24 recheck
    10. FFFF7BE2 must be 0

  NOTE ON CONDITION 7: FFFF7A20 is always 0.1 (written by clol_post_transition
  sub-A). 0.1 > 0.003906, so this condition may ALWAYS FAIL, which
  would mean AFL learning is permanently frozen. This needs further
  investigation — either:
    a) 0xBE608 implements an inverse comparison (value < threshold = fail)
    b) FFFF7A20 is modified by other code not yet traced
    c) The condition is checking abs(value - target) < threshold

  AFL LEARNING RATES:
    Airflow < 35.0 g/s (CC08C): delay counter threshold = 88 ticks
    Airflow >= 35.0 g/s: delay counter threshold = 244 ticks (~2.8x slower)
    Step size: 0.001 (CC05C) per update cycle
    Limits: +/- 25% (CC064/CC068)

  AFL STORAGE:
    4 learning values at FFFF316C + (range * 8):
      Range 0 (FFFF316C): 0 - 6.0 g/s (idle)
      Range 1 (FFFF3174): 6.0 - 23.0 g/s (light cruise)
      Range 2 (FFFF317C): 23.0 - 40.0 g/s (normal driving)
      Range 3 (FFFF3184): 40.0 - 80.0 g/s (heavy load, partially in OL)

  AFL APPLICATION (0x37B74):
    Reads interpolated AFL from FFFF31AC (primary) and FFFF31A4 (secondary)
    Computes multiplier using calibration weights CC2F4 and CC2FC
    Writes final multiplier to FFFF7AB4
    DOES NOT CHECK: FFFF7448 (CL/OL mode)
    DOES NOT CHECK: Current airflow against any max threshold
    Only checks: FFFF726C (transient flag), FFFF7C68 (status flag)
    Skip path writes 1.0 to FFFF7AB4 (no correction)

  FUEL PULSE WIDTH CALCULATION (0x0301E4):
    Reads FFFF7AB4 (AFL multiplier)
    Applies as direct multiplier to corrected base fuel value at 0x030230
    NO CL/OL check in fuel calc path


================================================================================
SECTION 8: MODIFIED ROM AFL CALIBRATION CHANGES
================================================================================

  +-----------------------------+----------+----------+--------------------------+
  | Parameter                   | Stock    | Modified | Effect                   |
  +-----------------------------+----------+----------+--------------------------+
  | CC074 (Range A breakpoint)  | 5.6 g/s  | 6.0 g/s  | Slightly higher idle     |
  | CC078 (Range B breakpoint)  | 10.0 g/s | 23.0 g/s | Much wider low range     |
  | CC07C (Range C breakpoint)  | 50.0 g/s | 40.0 g/s | OL learning boundary     |
  +-----------------------------+----------+----------+--------------------------+

  All other AFL calibration values are UNCHANGED from stock:
    CC020 = 70.0 g/s (learning max airflow)
    CC064 = -25% (min limit)
    CC068 = +25% (max limit)
    CC05C = 0.001 (step size)
    CC08C = 35.0 g/s (learning rate boundary)
    CC090 = 0.0 (Range D disabled)
    CC080 = 80.0 g/s (Range C high)


================================================================================
SECTION 9: ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS
================================================================================

  THE AFL LEAN CONDITION HAS THREE ROOT CAUSES:

  ROOT CAUSE 1 — AFL Application Has No CL/OL Gate:
    The AFL application function (0x37B74) applies the learned AFL
    multiplier to fueling regardless of whether the ECU is in CL or OL.
    This is stock Subaru behavior by design. In stock calibration this
    is less problematic because:
      - Stock OL thresholds are much higher (91% throttle, 4.8 g/rev load)
      - Transitions to OL happen at high RPM/load where AFL corrections
        are small
      - Stock hysteresis values are smaller, so return to CL is quicker

    In the modified calibration:
      - OL engages at 37.884% throttle and 0.95 g/rev load
      - AFL corrections learned during CL at moderate loads carry into OL
      - OL fuel maps assume no AFL correction, so the AFL trim creates
        a lean (or rich) offset that persists for the entire OL event

  ROOT CAUSE 2 — AFL Values Persist (No Reset on Transition):
    When CL->OL transition occurs:
      - AFL learning freezes (correct, function at 0x34C54 checks FFFF7448)
      - AFL stored values at FFFF316C-3184 are NOT zeroed
      - The last-learned values continue to be applied
    When OL->CL transition occurs:
      - AFL learning resumes from the previously stored values
      - The stale OL-period values gradually get updated by CL feedback

  ROOT CAUSE 3 — No Airflow-Based Application Cutoff:
    The user's CC07C=40.0 g/s defines the learning RANGE BOUNDARY, not
    an application cutoff. Above 40 g/s, the AFL function uses Range 3
    values (FFFF3184). If Range 3 has any learned correction, it gets
    applied above 40 g/s.

    The "A/F #1 Learning Max Threshold" parameter (which would provide
    an airflow-based application cutoff) exists in the 32BITBASE
    definition for newer ECU architectures but is NOT DEFINED and NOT
    PRESENT in the AE5L600L ROM. This ECU has no mechanism to disable
    AFL application based on airflow.


================================================================================
SECTION 10: THE "DELAY" MISCONCEPTION
================================================================================

  The perceived delay in CL->OL transition is NOT caused by the CL-to-OL
  delay parameter (CBC62=0). That parameter correctly zeroes counter_B,
  allowing immediate OL enrichment computation.

  The perceived delay is actually AFL persistence:

  Timeline of a WOT event:
    t=0.000s: Throttle exceeds 37.884 deg, condition checker fires
    t=0.000s: counter_B = 0, OL enrichment computed immediately (Path A)
    t=0.000s: FFFF7448 clears (Path B), AFC drops to 0
    t=0.000s: AFL learning freezes
    t=0.000s: AFL APPLICATION continues with last CL-learned values
    t=0.000s+: OL fuel = OL_map * (1.0 + AFL_trim_from_CL)
              If AFL_trim was -3%, OL fuel is 3% lean
    t=entire_event: AFL trim persists unchanged for entire OL event

  What the datalog shows as "AFL lingering" is the AFL correction value
  being APPLIED to fueling. It's not a transition delay — it's the
  normal behavior of this ECU applying learned corrections during OL.

  AFC drops immediately because it is directly gated by FFFF7448.
  AFL "lingers" because it has NO such gate.


================================================================================

================================================================================
SECTION 14: RECOMMENDATIONS
================================================================================

  OPTION A — Accept AFL in OL (Minimal Change):
    The stock ECU design intentionally applies AFL in OL. If your OL
    fuel maps are calibrated with AFL at zero, the AFL trim during OL
    is unwanted. But if calibrated with typical AFL values in mind,
    the trim is harmless.

    Action: Verify that OL fuel map targets account for typical AFL
    correction values. If AFL typically learns +/- 3%, build that
    margin into OL targets.

  OPTION B — Zero AFL Ranges for OL Airflows:
    Set the AFL Range C breakpoint (CC07C) back to a high value (e.g.,
    80+ g/s) so that all OL-relevant airflows fall in Range D (which
    is disabled at CC090=0.0). This prevents AFL from LEARNING values
    at airflows where you'll be in OL.

    Limitation: This doesn't prevent already-learned lower-range values
    from being interpolated/extrapolated into higher airflow zones.

  OPTION C — Widen AFL Step to Drain Faster (NOT RECOMMENDED):
    Increasing CC05C (step size) would make AFL update faster when
    returning to CL, but it won't help during OL events because
    learning is frozen. This doesn't address the root cause.

  OPTION D — ROM Patch: Gate AFL Application by FFFF7448:
    The most complete solution. Modify the AFL application function at
    0x37B74 to check FFFF7448 before writing the AFL multiplier.
    If FFFF7448 == 0 (OL mode), force FFFF7AB4 = 1.0 (no correction).

    Implementation sketch (SH-2 assembly):
      ; At 0x37B74 or before the FFFF7AB4 write:
      mov.l @(ptr_7448,PC),R2    ; load address of FFFF7448
      mov.b @R2,R0               ; read CL/OL flag
      tst R0,R0                  ; is it 0 (OL)?
      bf .cl_path                ; if nonzero (CL), apply AFL normally
      fldi1 FR0                  ; OL: force multiplier = 1.0
      mov.l @(ptr_7AB4,PC),R2   ; load address of FFFF7AB4
      fmov.s FR0,@R2            ; write 1.0 (no AFL correction)
      bra .skip_afl              ; skip normal AFL application
      nop
    .cl_path:
      ; ... existing AFL application code ...

    This patch would need to be placed in the ROM hole (0x0DB000+)
    with a branch from the original function.

  OPTION E — ROM Patch: Add Airflow Gate to AFL Application:
    Similar to Option D but adds an airflow comparison:
    If current_airflow > threshold, force FFFF7AB4 = 1.0.
    This gives you a configurable max airflow for AFL application
    without tying it strictly to the CL/OL flag.

  RECOMMENDED APPROACH: Option D is cleanest. It eliminates AFL
  influence during OL completely. Option B is the simplest no-patch
  approach but may not fully solve the problem due to interpolation.

================================================================================
SECTION 14B: OPTION D IMPACT / BRICK RISK ASSESSMENT
================================================================================

  SHORT ANSWER:
    Option D is generally a LOW brick-risk patch if implemented as a
    small logic gate in code RAM/ROM hole with a conservative branch
    hook and no changes to clocking, flash routines, watchdog control,
    or interrupt vectors.

  WHAT OPTION D CHANGES FUNCTIONALLY:
    - It changes ONLY AFL *application* behavior (FFFF7AB4 multiplier)
      when FFFF7448 indicates OL.
    - It does NOT change:
      * injector deadtime tables
      * base fuel map values
      * AFC PI control code
      * boost / ignition / knock logic
      * CL/OL decision logic itself (unless you intentionally do so)
    - Net effect: in OL, commanded fuel follows OL model without
      long-term trim carryover.

  POSSIBLE SIDE EFFECTS TO EXPECT (NON-BRICK):
    1) Seam behavior at CL->OL and OL->CL boundaries may change:
       removing AFL multiplier in OL can create a visible step if OL
       maps were previously tuned "with AFL in the loop".
    2) If OL maps are currently lean and AFL was masking it, AFR may
       shift richer or leaner depending on learned trim sign history.
    3) Transient fueling feel may change slightly in early boost
       because the multiplier path now hard-forces 1.0 in OL.

  TRUE BRICK RISK DRIVERS (WHAT ACTUALLY BRICKS ECUS):
    - Bad flash write (power interruption, cable disconnect, unstable
      voltage, wrong target ECU ID/segment).
    - Corrupt vector table / reset entry / checksum-critical regions.
    - Branch hook to invalid address, wrong instruction alignment, or
      clobbered register/FR state causing crash in scheduler context.
    - Patch overlap with other custom code in ROM hole.

  HOW TO KEEP OPTION D SAFE:
    1) Patch hygiene:
       - Preserve original overwritten instructions exactly in stub.
       - Save/restore any GPR/FPR/status bits your stub touches.
       - Keep stack usage minimal and deterministic.
       - Ensure branch target is 2-byte aligned and in reachable range.
    2) Flash hygiene:
       - Use a stable charger/power supply (no battery-only flashing).
       - Verify ROM ID and read-back compare after write.
       - Keep a known-good stock binary and recovery procedure ready.
    3) Calibration hygiene:
       - Start with wastegate spring / low boost validation pulls.
       - Monitor wideband AFR, IAM/knock correction, injector duty, EGT
         (if available), and commanded vs measured lambda.
       - Retune OL map and/or MAF scaling after patch if AFR shifts.

  PRACTICAL RECOMMENDATION:
    If your main goal is "no AFL effect in OL", Option D is the most
    deterministic method and safer from a drivability standpoint than
    trying to force table breakpoints to mimic a hard cutoff. The main
    risk is implementation quality, not the strategy itself.


================================================================================
SECTION 15: INTERRUPT ARCHITECTURE
================================================================================

  SH7058 INTERRUPT DISPATCH SYSTEM
  ---------------------------------
  The AE5L600L uses a single generic ISR entry point for ALL peripheral
  interrupts. This is the "common interrupt handler" scheme.

  INTERRUPT FLOW:
    1. Any peripheral IRQ fires (timer, ADC, SCI, CAN, etc.)
    2. CPU reads vector from VBR+0x2C = ROM 0x0002C = 0x0000BAC
    3. CPU jumps to isr_generic_handler (0x000BAC)
    4. Generic handler saves R0-R7, PR, MACH, MACL to stack
    5. Calls isr_dispatch_manager (0x000F4C) with R4=20
    6. Dispatch manager calls isr_intevt_resolver (0x000EE4) to
       identify which peripheral fired (reads INTEVT/priority register)
    7. Uses result as index into isr_dispatch_table (0x000E5EC)
    8. Jumps to specific ISR handler
    9. Returns, generic handler restores registers and issues RTE

  EXCEPTION VECTOR TABLE (ROM 0x000000-0x000033, VBR=0 at reset):
    0x0000  0x000C0C   initial PC = main code entry
    0x0004  0xFFFFBFA0 initial SP = RAM top (0xFFFF8000 + 0x3FA0)
    0x0008  0x000C0C   manual reset PC
    0x000C  0xFFFFBFA0 manual reset SP
    0x0010  0x000BFA   illegal instruction -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x0014  0x000BFA   illegal slot instruction -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x0018  0x000BFA   CPU address error -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x001C  0x000BFA   DMA bus error -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x0020  0x000BFA   NMI -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x0024  0x000BFA   user break -> exc_trap_infinite_loop
    0x002C  0x000BAC   ALL peripheral IRQs -> isr_generic_handler

  KEY ISR INFRASTRUCTURE ADDRESSES:
    0x000BAC  isr_generic_handler      Generic ISR entry (saves all regs, calls dispatch)
    0x000BF6  isr_generic_rte          RTE after register restore
    0x000BFA  exc_trap_infinite_loop   Exception trap (AFFE = BRA self)
    0x000F4C  isr_dispatch_manager     Identifies interrupt source, calls handler
    0x000EE4  isr_intevt_resolver      Reads INTEVT register, returns dispatch index
    0x000D78  isr_int_acknowledge      Interrupt acknowledge/clear
    0x000E5EC isr_dispatch_table       54 function pointers (4 bytes each)

  ISR DISPATCH TABLE (0x000E5EC, 54 entries x 4 bytes):
    Index  Handler     Identity
    -----  ----------  ----------------------------------------
    [  0]  0x010A46    isr_handler_0
    [  1]  0x00FC04    isr_handler_1
    [  2]  0x005840    isr_handler_2   (accesses MTU timer regs 0xFFFF4024)
    [  3]  0x00D658    isr_handler_3   (accesses MTU timer regs 0xFFFF4024)
    [  4]  0x00CBAC    isr_handler_4
    [  5]  0x04907C    isr_handler_5
    [  6]  0x009A58    isr_handler_6
    [  7]  0x00D268    isr_handler_7
    [  8]  0x00CBEE    isr_handler_8
    [  9]  0x0035A4    isr_handler_9
    [ 10]  0x00FE22    isr_handler_10
    [ 11]  0x00A878    isr_handler_11
    [ 12]  0x00D940    isr_handler_12
    [ 13]  0x009A14    isr_handler_13
    [ 14]  0x008528    isr_handler_14
    [ 15]  0x04A94C    isr_task_scheduler  *** task scheduler (59 tasks) ***
    [ 16]  0x04AA58    isr_handler_16
    [ 17]  0x009A34    isr_handler_17
    [ 18]  0x0085AC    isr_handler_18
    [ 19]  0x00D3DC    isr_handler_19
    [ 20]  0x010D58    isr_handler_20
    [ 21]  0x04793C    isr_rcan0           CAN controller ch0 (0xFFFF36BE/3D08)
    [ 22]  0x048732    isr_rcan1           CAN controller ch1 (same regs)
    [ 23]  0x01076A    isr_handler_23
    [ 24]  0x004BCA    isr_handler_24
    [ 25]  0x010124    isr_handler_25
    [ 26]  0x047B66    isr_handler_26
    [ 27]  0x049A7A    isr_handler_27
    [ 28]  0x00C36C    isr_handler_28   (accesses 0xFFFF4024)
    [ 29]  0x00A844    isr_handler_29
    [ 30]  0x049BA4    isr_handler_30
    [ 31]  0x00C370    isr_handler_31   (accesses 0xFFFF4024)
    [ 32]  0x005798    isr_handler_32
    [ 33]  0x049CF0    isr_handler_33
    [ 34]  0x00D4FC    isr_handler_34   (accesses 0xFFFF4024)
    [ 35]  0x00812C    isr_handler_35
    [ 36]  0x00ACFC    isr_handler_36
    [ 37]  0x04A03E    isr_handler_37

    [ 53]  0x04AE82    isr_handler_53

  NEXT STEPS FOR ISR IDENTIFICATION:
    - Trace 0xEE4 to understand how dispatch index maps to peripheral ID
    - Trace handlers that access 0xFFFF4024 (MTU timer regs) for crank/cam ISR
    - Identify ADC complete ISR (feeds rpm_current, ect_current, etc.)
    - Trace scheduler tick ISR (entry [15] = 0x4A94C) timing source

  CALIBRATION DESCRIPTOR LABELS (in ImportAE5L600L.java):
    All 760 calibration descriptors now labeled. Format: desc_<type>_<addr>
    Top groups:
      1D_ECT  (258): coolant temp lookup tables (most common)
      1D_RPM  (107): RPM-indexed tables
      1D_range (91): other axis types
      2D_LoadxRPM (49): 2D load x RPM tables (fuel/timing)
      1D_Throttle (41): throttle-indexed tables
      2D_range (29): other 2D tables
      1D_Boost (26): boost pressure tables
    Total: 621 1D + 139 2D = 760 descriptors


================================================================================
SECTION 16: OPEN QUESTIONS
================================================================================

  1. FFFF7A20 AND CL_ACTIVE_CHECK CONDITION 7:
     FFFF7A20 (blending rate) is always 0.1. The cl_active_check at
     0x345A4 passes this through 0xBE608 with threshold 0.003906.
     If 0xBE608 returns "fail" when value > threshold, then FFFF7A20=0.1
     would cause condition 7 to ALWAYS FAIL, meaning AFL learning is
     PERMANENTLY FROZEN. This contradicts the fact that AFL does learn
     in practice. Either:
       a) 0xBE608 returns "pass" when value > threshold (inverted)
       b) FFFF7A20 is modified by code we haven't traced
       c) 0xBE608 compares abs(value - 1.0) < threshold or similar
     Tracing 0xBE608 fully would resolve this.

  2. FFFF7452 MASTER READINESS TIMING:
     The master readiness flag at FFFF7452 (written at 0x031966) has
     its own conditions and hysteresis. The exact timing of this flag's
     response to CL/OL conditions has not been fully characterized.
     It affects how quickly FFFF7448 switches modes.

  3. TRANSIENT FLAG FFFF726C:
     This flag gates AFL application. If it is set during WOT/rapid
     throttle changes, it would temporarily disable AFL application
     (write 1.0 to FFFF7AB4). The duration and conditions for this
     flag have not been traced. If it stays active long enough, it
     could partially mask the AFL persistence issue during the initial
     transition, then clear (allowing AFL to resume) after things
     stabilize — which could look like a "delayed" AFL return.


================================================================================
END OF ANALYSIS
================================================================================
